< Text>
Alexan in terms of beauty and appeal is the nicest building in East Village, perhaps even all of Downtown SD. I have been here for 2 years and over the past 6 months, this place has really displayed it's cracks. I''ll explain:

Firstly, the head leasing agent never replies to E'mail's and I have spoke to numerous tenants about this same issue.

In an effort to be more "green" Alexan removed the plastic coffee cups entirely. They came up with no alternative so either you come down with a thermus every-time or you just don't have coffee period. If you have guests and they want a cup of coffee, you better have a spare thermus for your friend. It's crazy to think of a building that prides itself to be so ritzy and glamours... and they can't even supply coffee cups to tenants who pay so much rent. Motel 6 offers their guests coffee cups.

It took 3 months for Alexan to fix the 2nd shutter gate. They were motivated to do so because we have had multiple car breakin's and thievery in the parking structure. Not to mention, a month before that we had hundreds of packages stolen from our mailbox room. How you ask? Easy, there is a mailbox room located in the garage with no surveillance camera's at all; the whole garage structure has no camera's so the building has no idea who is coming in and out by surveillance footage.

The management team also gave up on community events. Expect maybe 1 event a month; even with that number I'm overestimating.

2 months ago Alexan decides to hit us with a whole new parking system handled by a 3rd party company. This further separates tenants from the leasing agents because they can't help or handle any situations regrading the parking garage at all now.

In conclusion, Alexan's rent is probably $200-300 more than the surrounding competition. The high rent fees here really don't give you that extra luxury you would expect; As a matter of fact, it falls short.  It's probably a smarter move to save your hundreds of hard earned dollars a month and find a place that is more secure,  has coffee cups, and can provide better assistance to tenants when needed.<//Text>

<gmapID>0x80d954e876536823:0x62dc2e4dd23e8514< /gmapID>< text>
I was referred to Project Trans @ The Center, by my Doctor. As a transgender woman, just beginning my transition, I was in search for any help, resources and guidance, I could get. I have definitely gotten that from Project Trans @The Center.

I was hesitant to reach out at first, as I was not yet publicly out to most friends and family. After a few weeks, I decided to finally reach out. I decided my comfort level was to reach out to them, via email. After sending an email, I received an email reply within 1 day, from Karrah.

Karrah's email was warm and welcoming. She explained the services they provided and offered to set up an intake appointment to get me started. As this was all new to me, I was a bit nervous going in for my appointment. When I arrived, I checked in at the front desk. I was greeted by everyone at the front desk, they were all friendly and that made me feel at ease. My appointment with Karrah lasted about 30min total.

Karrah was friendly, welcoming and respectful. I immediately felt comfortable after meeting with her. Karrah was able to set me up with therapy sessions, which they provided, as well contact information for their Transgender Services Coordinator, Naya. As an added comfort level, they do ask you if you have any preferences (male/female) you may have when setting you up with the right therapist.

I have been seeing my Therapist, Tanesha for a few months now. I could not have been paired with anyone better than her. She has been a saving grace and I enjoy being able to see her.

I also reached out to their Transgender Services Coordinator, Naya. In regards to getting assistance on changing my name and gender marker, legally. Naya contacted me via telephone and couldn't have been anymore respectful and welcoming. She was so friendly and eager to help me. She asked a few questions to better get to know me and what it was I was looking for. I let her know I was wanting to change my legal name and gender marker and that I wasn't sure where to start in that process. She then set me up for an 1 on 1 appointment, with her.

When I arrived for my appointment with Naya, I felt at ease with her. She helped me fill out all the required forms, to start the process, of legally changing my name/gender marker. She was a breath of fresh air, as she knows exactly how to assist me, being a transwoman herself. Naya was able to help me in getting a waiver with the courts filing fee, which was such a huge help. After helping me get all the forms I needed, she gave me a step by step guide on what to do from that point on. This guide assisted me with contact and address information to the San Diego Courthouse, which room to bring my paperwork to and any information and/or documents I should bring with me, to file my paperwork. This was so helpful, when I arrived at the San Diego Courthouse. Naya was available to answer questions I had after our appointment and has been such a wonderful experience for me.

My name and gender marker are now successfully and legally changed!

Everyone at Project Trans and The Center have been nothing short of amazing and helpful. I'm so thankful to each and every one of them, from the intake, to the services and people they provided.  I definitely recommend anyone who is seeking assistance to reach out to them.<//text>

Now I can understand human error and can understand something being missed but 3 huge errors like this is unacceptable. 1) my car was in their care for over a month and any decent mechanic knows that batteries need to be maintained, 2) we brought them an overheating vehicle with a huge coolant leak and it was returned with no coolant!, and 3) a huge plastic piece was missing from the underside of the car in which they asked us 3 times if we took off. This service department is completely incompetent and once we get our car back we will not be coming back.

Update: Chevy gave us a used battery. For that I'll add another star</Review>

Their first offer on a 22k car was $700 a month over 72 mo. They told me it was a great deal. As someone who worked in financing I knew how ridiculous the deal was and got up to walk out. They persuaded me to stay and gave me 3 more offers before offering a payment that was even on the edges of acceptability. They told me every time that it was a great deal.

On top of that, they consistently tried to avoid the negotiation on the sticker price that was already ridiculously high. It was a struggle to start that discussion before the financing discussion and it took a long time to get them to start talking.

I entered the dealer at 4:30PM and left at 12:30AM . The negotiation took that long. After having the used car for two days I noticed there were no floor mats, the tires on the front and rear were different manufacturers, and there were spots worked over with touch up paint. When I contacted the sales person he said, "As Is." They did absolutely nothing to show they were interested in the welfare of their costumers. From offering ludicrous financing to no post customer help they were horrible. I received my tags and licenses today and I was elated to take their registration sticker from my windshield.

For anyone looking to purchase a car, look elsewhere. This dealers business practices are far beyond the typical predatory nature of most car dealerships.

*They didn't smog the used vehicle and two months after purchase notified me to drive 40 mi to them from where I work and live so that they could finish the registration process. When I showed up they sent me to a local gas station instead of handling it themselves.< /text>
